OVERVIEW\n52: \n53: ### What This Framework Does\n54: \n55: AI coding assistants have amnesia. Every session starts from zero. You explain your architecture Monday. By Wednesday, it is gone. Decisions, trade-offs, the carefully reasoned choices behind them, all lost the moment the conversation window closes. This framework fixes that.\n56: \n57: The framework adds four layers on top of the base platform:\n58: \n59: 1. **Structured documentation** (Spec Kit) - every file change gets a spec folder recording what changed, why and how. Like a lab notebook for software.\n60: 2. **Cognitive memory** (MCP server) - a local-first memory engine storing decisions, context and project history in a searchable database. Like a personal librarian who remembers every conversation.\n61: 3. **Code intelligence** (Code Graph + CocoIndex) - structural graph indexing handles callers, imports and impact analysis, while semantic search finds code by concept.\n62: 4. **Coordinated agents and skills** - 11 specialized agents routed by a gate system that loads the right skills at the right time.\n63: \n64: |                        |                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |\n65: | ---------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n66: | **­¤ż¢ 11 Agents**        | 11 custom specialists, multi-runtime                                                                                                                                                                                                              |\n67: | **­¤Ä» 21 Skills**        | Code, docs, git, prompts, MCP, research, review, council, improvement, cross-AI, small-model sentinel, and standalone system packages                                                                                                              |\n68: | **Ōī©’ĖÅ 22 Commands**      | 6 spec_kit + 4 memory + 6 create + 2 improve + 3 doctor + 1 agent_router                                                                                                                                                                          |\n69: | **­¤ö¦ 69 MCP Tools**     | mk-spec-memory (39), mk_skill_advisor (9), mk_code_index (11), code mode (7), CocoIndex (2), sequential thinking (1). See canonical count in FAQ                                                                            |\n70: | **­¤öŹ CocoIndex Code**   | [Forked](.opencode/skills/mcp-coco-index/NOTICE) from [cocoindex-io/cocoindex-code](https://github.com/cocoindex-io/cocoindex-code) (Apache 2.0) - semantic code search via vector embeddings and natural-language discovery across 28+ languages |\n71: | **­¤ÅŚ’ĖÅ Code Graph**       | First-class skill at [`.opencode/skills/system-code-graph/`](.opencode/skills/system-code-graph/) with standalone MCP server identity `mk_code_index` and client namespace `mcp__mk_code_index__*`                                               |\n72: | **ŌÜĪ Runtime Coverage** | OpenCode, Codex CLI (requires `[features].codex_hooks = true` opt-in for native hooks), Claude Code, Gemini CLI, plus Copilot CLI startup-surface support (file-based custom instructions)                                                        |\n73: \n74: ### How It All ### What's Shipped Recently\n127: \n128: The code graph now lives in `.opencode/skills/system-code-graph/` with its own MCP boundary. A follow-on rename established `mk_code_index` as the standalone server identity and `mcp__mk_code_index__*` as the live documentation namespace.\n129: \n130: Recent work also tightened the public surface without turning this README into a changelog: CocoIndex now has a canonical feature inventory, stress coverage is aligned, and the local llama-cpp path has stronger embedding failure reporting plus token-aware truncation.\n131: \n132: ### Embedder Architecture\n133: \n134: Both native MCPs are pluggable out of the box, no code change to swap. **mk-spec-memory** defaults to `nomic-embed-text-v1.5` (768 dim, Ollama-served) per ADR-013/014 local-first cascade (2026-05-19); `jina-embeddings-v3` (1024 dim) is the second-priority fallback. The retrieval-rescue layer is default-on per ADR-011 (kill switch: `SPECKIT_RERANK_LAYER=false`). **CocoIndex** ships a two-stage pipeline: Stage 1 embedder default `sbert/nomic-ai/CodeRankEmbed` (768 dim, MIT, code-tuned bi-encoder, MPS auto-detect on Apple Silicon ŌĆö promoted 2026-05-19); Stage 2 cross-encoder reranker default `Qwen/Qwen3-Reranker-0.6B` (Apache-2.0 ŌĆö promoted 2026-05-20 per ADR-027 after a head-to-head bench against jina-reranker-v3, which is kept as opt-in fallback). The Code Graph rides on CocoIndex's embedder choice via a shared bridge. See the canonical narrative at [embedder-pluggability.md](.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/references/embedder-pluggability.md) and the swap runbook in [CocoIndex INSTALL_GUIDE ┬¦4 \"Choosing an embedder\"](.opencode/skills/mcp-coco-index/INSTALL_GUIDE.md).\n135: \n136: <!-- /ANCHOR:overview -->\n137: \n138: \n139: <!-- ANCHOR:quick-start -->\n140: \n141: ---\n142: \n143: ## 2. QUICK START\n144: \n145: ### Installation\n146: \n147: **Prerequisites:** Node.js 18+ with `npm`, `git` and a POSIX shell. The launcher binaries vendor their own dependencies on first run, so you do not need TypeScript or `tsc` installed globally.\n148: \n149: ```bash\n150: # 1. Clone the repository\n151: git clone https://github.com/MichelKerkmeester/opencode--spec-kit-skilled-agent-orchestration.git\n152: cd opencode--spec-kit-skilled-agent-orchestration\n153: \n154: # 2. Install root dependencies (file watcher + shared HTTP utilities)\n155: npm install\n156: \n157: # 3. Boot the native MCP servers via their committed launchers\n158: # Each launcher is a self-contained .cjs that vendors its own deps on first run.\n159: node .opencode/bin/mk-spec-memory-launcher.cjs --help\n160: node .opencode/bin/mk-skill-advisor-launcher.cjs --help\n161: node .opencode/bin/mk-code-index-launcher.cjs --help\n162: \n163: # 4. (Optional) Install the CocoIndex Code soft-fork for semantic code search\n164: bash .opencode/skills/mcp-coco-index/scripts/install.sh\n165: ```\n166: \n167: The native MCP servers (`mk-spec-memory`, `mk_skill_advisor`, `mk_code_index`) ship as committed launcher binaries under `.opencode/bin/`. They self-vendor their dependencies on first invocation and the checked-in runtime configs already point at them. There is no separate build step.\n168: \n169: ### Set Up Embedding Provider\n170: \n171: Choose an embedding provider:\n172: \n173: ```bash\n174: # Default when no cloud keys are set: nomic-embed-text-v1.5 (768 dim)\n175: # served by a local Ollama HTTP endpoint. Pull the model once:\n176: #   ollama pull nomic-embed-text:v1.5\n177: # (jina-embeddings-v3 is the second-priority fallback; pull via:\n178: #   ollama pull hf.co/gaianet/jina-embeddings-v3-GGUF:Q4_K_M)\n179: \n180: # Option A: Voyage AI (cloud, requires API key, opt-in only)\n181: export VOYAGE_API_KEY=\"your-key-here\"\n182: \n183: # Option B: OpenAI embeddings (cloud, requires API key)\n184: export OPENAI_API_KEY=\"your-key-here\"\n185: \n186: # Option C: HuggingFace Local (free, CPU/ONNX fallback when Ollama is unavailable)\n187: # Auto-detected when the Ollama probe fails and no cloud keys are set\n188: ```\n189: \n190: ### Verify Installation\n191: \n192: ```bash\n193: # Confirm the launcher binaries respond\n194: node .opencode/bin/mk-spec-memory-launcher.cjs --help\n195: node .opencode/bin/mk-skill-advisor-launcher.cjs --help\n196: node .opencode/bin/mk-code-index-launcher.cjs --help\n197: \n198: # Confirm the active runtime's MCP config references the launchers\n199: # (only the runtime you use needs to exist. .codex/config.toml ships in the repo)\n200: grep -l 'mk-spec-memory\\|mk_skill_advisor\\|mk_code_index' \\\n201:   opencode.json .claude/mcp.json .codex/config.toml .gemini/settings.json 2>/dev/null\n202: ```\n203: \n204: ### First Use\n205: \n206: Open OpenCode in your project directory. The framework is active. Try:\n207: \n208: ```\n209: /spec_kit:complete Build a user authentication system\n210: ```\n211: \n212: This creates a spec folder, runs research, builds a plan and begins implementation - all with memory saved automatically. When you come back tomorrow, the memory engine remembers everything.\n213: \n214: ### Adapting to Your Stack\n215: \n216: This repo ships as a public template. Of the shipped skills, `sk-code` carries the stack-specific patterns (frontend framework, animation library, CMS, backend language). Start there when forking. The other shipped skills (`system-spec-kit`, `sk-doc`, `sk-git`, `sk-code-review`, `mcp-coco-index`, the deep-research/deep-review loops, the `cli-*` orchestrators) are codebase-agnostic out of the box and work for any project without modification. Most teams will also add their own skills on top. Drop them into `.opencode/skills/<your-skill>/` and they'll be picked up automatically.\n217: \n218: See [┬¦4 Customizing for Your Stack](#customizing-for-your-stack) for the full customization map and step-by-step adaptation guide.\n219: \n220: ### Code-Graph Indexing\n221: \n222: The standalone `mk_code_index` MCP server indexes **your project's production code** by default, not the framework backend. End users inherit this behavior automatically through the committed config defaults. See [┬¦4 Maintainer-Mode Code-Graph Flags](#maintainer-mode-code-graph-flags-already-disabled-for-end-users) only if you're contributing upstream.\n223: \n224: <!-- /ANCHOR:quick-start -->\n225: \n226: \n227: <!-- ANCHOR:features -->\n228: \n229: ---\n230: \n231: ## 3. FEATURES\n232: \n233: ### ­¤ōŗ Spec Kit Documentation\n234: \n235: The Spec Kit enforces structured spec folders for every file-modifying conversation. Gate 3 requires a spec folder answer before any file modification begins (only typo/whitespace fixes under 5 characters are exempt).\n236: \n237: #### Documentation Levels\n238: \n239: Documentation depth scales with task complexity.\n240: \n241: | Level  | LOC Guidance   | Required Files                                                          | When to Use                                                              |\n242: | ------ | -------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------ |\n243: | **1**  | < 100          | spec.md, plan.md, tasks.md, implementation-summary.md                   | Small features, bug fixes, single-file changes                           |\n244: | **2**  | 100 - 499      | Level 1 + checklist.md                                                  | Features needing QA verification, multi-file changes                     |\n245: | **3**  | 500+           | Level 2 + decision-record.md                                            | Architecture changes, complex refactors                                  |\n246: | **3+** | Complexity 80+ | Level 3 + approval workflow, compliance checkpoints, stakeholder matrix | High-complexity work needing review tracking and workstream coordination |\n247: \n248: The LOC ranges are guidance, not hard rules. Risk, complexity and the number of affected files can push a task to a higher level. When in doubt, choose the higher level.\n249: \n250: **Implementation-summary.md** is required at all levels but created **after** implementation completes, not at spec folder creation time.\n251: \n252: &nbsp;\n253: #### Spec Folder Structure\n254: \n255: ```text\n256: specs/<###-feature-name>/\n257: Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ description.json             # Spec identity and memory tracking metadata\n258: Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ spec.md                      # What the feature is and why it exists\n259: Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ plan.md                      # How to implement it\n260: Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ tasks.md                     # Step-by-step task breakdown\n261: Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ checklist.md                 # QA validation gates (Level 2+)\n262: Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ decision-record.md           # Architecture decisions (Level 3+)\n263: Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ implementation-summary.md    # Post-implementation summary (all levels)\n264: Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ resource-map.md              # Optional path ledger of resources the packet touched\n265: Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ graph-metadata.json          # Packet-level graph metadata (auto-refreshed on save)\n266: ŌööŌöĆŌöĆ scratch/                     # Temporary workspace files\n267: ```\n268: \n269: `resource-map.md` is optional at any level. Render it from `.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/templates/manifest/resource-map.md.tmpl` when a packet wants a lean, central listing of the files, scripts and external resources it interacts with. Deep-research and deep-review loops emit it automatically next to `review-report.md`.\n270: \n271: &nbsp;\n272: #### Checklist Priority System\n273: \n274: Checklists use a priority system so reviewers know what blocks shipping and what can wait:\n275: \n276: - **P0** - Hard blocker. Cannot ship without this. Cannot defer.\n277: - **P1** - Required. Must complete or get explicit user approval to defer.\n278: - **P2** - Optional. Nice to have. Can defer without approval.\n279: \n280: &nbsp;\n281: #### Phase Decomposition\n282: \n283: Phase decomposition splits large features into a parent spec folder (overall specification) and child folders (one per phase).\n284: \n285: ```text\n286: specs/022-big-feature/             # Parent spec folder\n287: Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ spec.md                        # Overall specification\n288: Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ 001-data-model/                # Phase 1 child\n289: Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ spec.md\n290: Ōöé   ŌööŌöĆŌöĆ ...\n291: Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ 002-api-endpoints/             # Phase 2 child\n292: Ōöé   Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ spec.md\n293: Ōöé   ŌööŌöĆŌöĆ ...\n294: ŌööŌöĆŌöĆ 003-frontend/                  # Phase 3 child\n295:     Ōö£ŌöĆŌöĆ spec.md\n296:     ŌööŌöĆŌöĆ ...\n297: ```\n298: \n299: Use `create.sh --phase` to create a parent with its first child in one step. Run `validate.sh --recursive` to validate the parent and all children together.\n300: \n301: &nbsp;\n302: #### Validation\n303: \n304: The `validate.sh` script runs 20 rules against a spec folder and reports what passes and what needs fixing. Rules check for required files, template compliance, placeholder detection, anchor markers and cross-reference consistency.\n305: \n306: - **Exit 0** - All rules pass. Ready to proceed.\n307: - **Exit 1** - User error (bad flags or invalid input).\n308: - **Exit 2** - Validation error. Must fix before claiming completion.\n309: - **Exit 3** - System error (file I/O failure, missing manifest or other environment problem).\n310: \n311: Run with `--verbose` to see details behind each rule or `--recursive` to validate a parent and all child phase folders. Strict validation of a Level 3 packet runs in ~108 ms via a single-orchestrator design. The default scaffold path skips post-create validation. Set `SPECKIT_POST_VALIDATE=1` to enable it for strict CI workflows. Path traversal inputs (e.g. `--path \"../etc/passwd\"`) are rejected before any filesystem write. Parallel `/memory:save` calls for the same packet are serialized by an advisory lock on `description.json` and `graph-metadata.json`.\n312: \n313: &nbsp;\n314: #### Scripts and Validation\n315: \n316: **Spec Management Scripts** (in `.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/scripts/spec/`):\n317: \n318: - **`create.sh`** - Create spec folders with level-appropriate templates. Use `--phase` for parent + child\n319: - **`validate.sh`** - Run 20 validation rules. Use `--recursive` for phase folders\n320: - **`upgrade-level.sh`** - Upgrade a spec folder to a higher level by injecting new sections\n321: - **`recommend-level.sh`** - Analyze scope and risk to recommend the right documentation level\n322: - **`calculate-completeness.sh`** - Calculate spec folder completeness as a percentage\n323: - **`check-completion.sh`** - Verify all completion criteria are met\n324: - **`check-placeholders.sh`** - Find remaining `[PLACEHOLDER]` values after level upgrade\n325: \n326: **Memory Scripts** (in `.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/scripts/memory/`):\n327: \n328: - **`generate-context.ts`** - Primary workflow for updating packet continuity and supporting generated context artifacts\n329: - **`backfill-frontmatter.ts`** - Add missing frontmatter to existing generated context artifacts and indexed spec docs\n330: - **`reindex-embeddings.ts`** - Rebuild embedding vectors for stored memories\n331: - **`cleanup-orphaned-vectors.ts`** - Remove vector entries with no matching memory\n332: - **`rebuild-auto-entities.ts`** - Regenerate auto-extracted entity catalog\n333: - **`validate-memory-quality.ts`** - Run quality checks on stored memory content\n334: \n335: TypeScript sources compile to `.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/scripts/dist/`. The runtime entry point for memory saves is `.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/scripts/dist/memory/generate-context.js`.\n336: \n337: &nbsp;\n338: #### Gate System\n339: \n340: 3 mandatory gates run before any file change. Every request passes through the same sequence.\n341: \n342: ```\n343:   User message arrives\n344:          Ōöé\n345:          Ō¢╝\n346:   ŌöīŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöÉ\n347:   Ōöé  Gate 1: Understanding (SOFT BLOCK)         Ōöé\n348:   Ōöé  memory_match_triggers() surfaces context   Ōöé\n349:   Ōöé  Classify intent: Research / Implementation Ōöé\n350:   Ōöé  confidence >= 0.70, uncertainty <= 0.35     Ōöé\n351: Ō¢╝\n354:   ŌöīŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöÉ\n355:   Ōöé  Gate 2: Skill Routing (REQUIRED)           Ōöé\n356:   Ōöé  advisor_recommend recommends skill         Ōöé\n357:   Ōöé  confidence >= 0.8 ŌöĆŌ¢║ MUST load skill        Ōöé\n358:   ŌööŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌö¼ŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöś\n359:                      Ōöé\n360:                      Ō¢╝\n361:   ŌöīŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöÉ\n362:   Ōöé  Gate 3: Spec Folder (HARD BLOCK)           Ōöé\n363:   Ōöé  Only if file modification detected           Ōöé\n364:   Ōöé  A) Existing  B) New  C) Update             Ōöé\n365:   Ōöé  D) Skip      E) Phase folder               Ōöé\n366:   ŌööŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌö¼ŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöś\n367:                      Ōöé\n368:                      Ō¢╝\n369:               EXECUTION\n370:                      Ōöé\n371:                      Ō¢╝\n372:   ŌöīŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöÉ\n373:   Ōöé  Post-Rules                                 Ōöé\n374:   Ōöé  Memory Save ŌöĆ must use generate-context.js Ōöé\n375:   Ōöé  Completion ŌöĆ verify checklist.md items     Ōöé\n376:   ŌööŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöś\n377: ```\n378: \n379: **Analysis Lenses** - applied silently on every request:\n380: - **CLARITY** - Is this the simplest solution? Are abstractions earned?\n381: - **SYSTEMS** - What does this touch? What are the side effects?\n382: - **BIAS** - Is the user solving a symptom? Is the framing correct?\n383: - **SUSTAINABILITY** - Will future developers understand this?\n384: - **VALUE** - Does this change behavior or just refactor?\n385: - **SCOPE** - Does solution complexity match problem size?\n386: \n387: For the full spec folder workflow, Level contract template architecture, gate definitions and anti-pattern detection rules, see the [ŌåÆ Spec Kit README](.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/README.md) and [ŌåÆ AGENTS.md](AGENTS.md).\n388: \n389: ---\n390: \n391: ### ­¤¦Ā Memory Engine\n392: \n393: The Memory Engine is a local-first cognitive memory system built as an MCP server. `generate-context.js` updates canonical packet continuity and may emit supporting generated context artifacts inside the spec folder. Canonical continuity lives in the spec packet itself: use `/spec_kit:resume` as the recovery surface, then rebuild context in this order: `handover.md` -> `_memory.continuity` -> canonical spec docs. The MCP server indexes those packet-local sources with vector embeddings, BM25 and FTS5 full-text search. `memory_match_triggers()` can still surface relevant prior context automatically when deeper retrieval is needed.\n394: \n395: `/memory:save` refreshes packet metadata on every invocation. `session_resume` binds `args.sessionId` to transport caller context by default. Set `MCP_SESSION_RESUME_AUTH_MODE=permissive` for rollout canaries. Copilot, Claude and Gemini all share the same compact-cache provenance path.\n396: \n397: The memory engine works with session lifecycle surfaces and hybrid retrieval. Structural code indexing now lives in the standalone [`system-code-graph`](.opencode/skills/system-code-graph/) skill and MCP server.\n398: \n399: Expired ephemeral rows are cleaned by a retention sweep on startup and hourly by default. Use `memory_retention_sweep` for manual or dry-run cleanup. The handler is defined at [memory-retention-sweep.ts](.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/handlers/memory-retention-sweep.ts), with `SPECKIT_RETENTION_SWEEP` and `SPECKIT_RETENTION_SWEEP_INTERVAL_MS` controlling the background interval.\n400: \n401: The full MCP API reference is in the [MCP Server README](.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/README.md).\n402: \n403: &nbsp;\n404: #### Layered MCP Surface\n405: \n406: The `mk-spec-memory` tools are organized into a layered architecture. Code graph and skill-advisor tools moved to standalone MCP servers, so this table covers memory-owned tools only:\n407: \n408: | Layer  | Name            | Tools  | Token Budget | Purpose                                                                      |\n409: | ------ | --------------- | ------ | ------------ | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n410: | **L1** | Orchestration   | 3      | 2,000        | Unified context, resume and bootstrap entry points                           |\n411: | **L2** | Core            | 3      | 1,500        | Search, trigger matching, save                                               |\n412: | **L3** | Discovery       | 4      | 800          | List, stats, health checks and session readiness                             |\n413: | **L4** | Mutation        | 5      | 500          | Delete, update, validate, bulk cleanup, retention sweep                      |\n414: | **L5** | Lifecycle       | 4      | 600          | Checkpoints and lifecycle state                                              |\n415: | **L6** | Analysis        | 7      | 1,200        | Causal graph (link/stats/drift_why), epistemic baselines, evaluations, dashboards |\n416: | **L7** | Maintenance     | 5      | 1,000        | Memory index scans, async ingest and learning history                        |\n417: | **L8** | Moved Surfaces  | 0      | -            | Code graph lives in `mk_code_index`. Advisor and skill graph live in `mk_skill_advisor` |\n418: | **L9** | Coverage Graph  | 4      | 700          | Deep-loop coverage graph operations                                          |\n419: | **L9** | Council Graph   | 4      | 700          | Deep AI Council graph operations                                             |\n420: |        | **Total**       | **39** | **~10,180**  |                                                                              |\n421: \n422: Lower layers load only when needed. L1 is always available. L2 loads for any search. L3-L7 load based on the specific command being used.\n423: \n424: &nbsp;\n425: #### Hybrid Search\n426: \n427: Every search checks five core channels at once, with CocoIndex available as a semantic code search bridge:\n428: \n429: - **Vector** - Semantic similarity via embeddings. Finds related content when words differ.\n430: - **FTS5** - Full-text search on exact words and phrases.\n431: - **BM25** - Keyword relevance scoring.\n432: - **Causal Graph** - Follows cause-and-effect links between memories.\n433: - **Degree** - Scores by graph connectivity, weighted by edge type.\n434: \n435: **Reciprocal Rank Fusion (RRF)** combines results across channels so memories scoring well in multiple channels rise to the top. **Graph-first routing** dispatches structural queries to the standalone Code Graph first, then CocoIndex for semantic code discovery, then the memory pipeline. A **3-tier FTS fallback** activates when graph and semantic channels miss: FTS5 full-text, BM25 keyword scoring, then Grep/Glob filesystem search. The system truncates weak results and ensures every active channel is represented.\n436: \n437: &nbsp;\n438: #### Search Pipeline\n439: \n440: Every search passes through 4 stages:\n441: \n442: - **Candidate generation** - Parallel retrieval from the active channels plus constitutional injection where applicable.\n443: - **Fusion** - RRF-based scoring with post-fusion signals such as co-activation, FSRS decay, interference control, intent weights and graph/session boosts when enabled.\n444: - **Rerank** - Cross-encoder reranking with chunk reassembly, a minimum Stage 3 gate of 4 candidates and compatibility-only length-penalty wiring that resolves to a neutral `1.0` multiplier. `getRerankerStatus()` exposes latency plus cache hits, misses, stale hits and evictions. If the reranker is unavailable, Stage 2 order is preserved with degraded metadata.\n445: - **Filtering** - State/quality filtering, confidence annotation, token-budget enforcement and final response shaping without mutating post-rerank scores.\n446: \n447: &nbsp;\n448: #### Query Intelligence\n449: \n450: - **Complexity routing** - Simple (2 channels), moderate (4), complex (all 5)\n451: - **Intent classification** - 7 public types (`add_feature`, `fix_bug`, `refactor`, `security_audit`, `understand`, `find_spec`, `find_decision`) plus an internal continuity profile for resume-oriented retrieval (`semantic 0.52`, `keyword 0.18`, `recency 0.07`, `graph 0.23`. Stage 3 MMR lambda `0.65`)\n452: - **Query decomposition** - Multi-topic queries split into sub-queries, expanded with related terms\n453: - **Context pressure** - Downgrades search mode at 60% and 80% window usage\n454: - **Fallback strategies** - LLM reformulation or HyDE for low-confidence searches\n455: \n456: Four response modes: **quick** (top answer only), **focused** (one-topic), **deep** (full evidence trails), **resume** (state summary + next-steps).\n457: \n458: &nbsp;\n459: #### Memory Lifecycle\n460: \n461: Memories fade using **FSRS** (Free Spaced Repetition Scheduler). Decay speed varies by content type and importance tier. Critical decisions never fade. Temporary debugging notes fade within days.\n462: \n463: - **Cold-start boost** - Fresh memories (under 48h) receive a temporary scoring lift\n464: - **Interference penalty** - Suppresses near-duplicate clusters\n465: - **Auto-promotion** - Memories earn higher tiers through positive validation\n466: - **Negative feedback** - 30-day decay prevents permanent blacklisting\n467: \n468: Four active cognitive states drive normal retrieval weighting: **HOT** >> **WARM** >> **COLD** >> **DORMANT**.\n469: \n470: &nbsp;\n471: #### Causal Graph\n472: \n473: Six relationship types: `caused`, `enabled`, `supersedes`, `contradicts`, `derived_from`, `supports`\n474: \n475: - **Typed traversal** - Prioritizes connection types based on query intent\n476: - **Community detection** - Louvain clustering with neighbor boosting\n477: - **Co-activation spreading** - Fan-effect dampening prevents hub bias\n478: - **Temporal contiguity** - Same-session grouping\n479: - **Graph momentum** - Trending knowledge surfaces higher\n480: - **LLM backfill** - Background discovery of missed causal links\n481: \n482: &nbsp;\n483: #### Trust Badges on Search Results\n484: \n485: Every search result ships with a small `trustBadges` block that tells you how reliable the hit is at a glance. The badges are display-only, they read existing causal links and don't add new storage:\n486: \n487: | Badge                  | What it tells you                                         |\n488: | ---------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------- |\n489: | `confidence`           | How strong the strongest causal link to this result is    |\n490: | `extractionAge`        | How long ago the supporting evidence was extracted        |\n491: | `lastAccessAge`        | How recently anything in the chain was used               |\n492: | `orphan`               | True when nothing else in the graph points at this result |\n493: | `weightHistoryChanged` | True when the underlying edge weight has been re-tuned    |\n494: \n495: If the database is unreachable the formatter quietly skips badges instead of failing. Caller-provided badges pass through untouched. Every response profile (`quick`, `research`, `resume`) keeps the badges on the top result and the result list.\n496: \n497: &nbsp;\n498: #### Save Intelligence\n499: \n500: When you save new knowledge, **Prediction Error gating** compares it against existing memories and picks one of four outcomes:\n501: \n502: - **CREATE** - No similar memory exists. Stored as new knowledge.\n503: - **REINFORCE** - Similar exists, new one adds value. Both kept, old one boosted.\n504: - **UPDATE** - Similar exists, new one is better. Old version replaced.\n505: - **SUPERSEDE** - New knowledge contradicts the old. Old one demoted to deprecated.\n506: \n507: Additional save-time processing:\n508: \n509: - **Semantic sufficiency gating** - Rejects content too thin to be useful\n510: - **Verify-fix-verify** - Auto-fixes quality issues before storing\n511: - **Content normalization** - Strips formatting clutter for cleaner embeddings\n512: - **Auto-entity extraction** - Spots tool/project/concept names for cross-linking\n513: - **SHA-256 deduplication** - Skips unchanged files instantly\n514: - **Correction tracking** - Records how knowledge evolves across versions\n515: \n516: &nbsp;\n517: #### Session Awareness\n518: \n519: - **Working memory** - Tracks current session findings with attention decay\n520: - **Session deduplication** - Suppresses already-seen results in follow-up queries\n521: - **Context pressure** - Downgrades search mode as the context window fills\n522: \n523: &nbsp;\n524: #### Quality Gates\n525: \n526: Three layered checks before storage:\n527: \n528: - **Structure gate** - Format, headings, metadata validation\n529: - **Semantic sufficiency** - Enough real content to be useful\n530: - **Duplicate detection** - Triggers Prediction Error arbitration if similar content exists\n531: \n532: Preview all checks without saving using `dryRun: true`. Learned relevance feedback boosts helpful results with safeguards against noise. Two-tier explainability shows plain-language reasons or exact channel contributions.\n533: \n534: &nbsp;\n535: #### Retrieval Enhancements\n536: \n537: - **Constitutional injection** - Always-surfaced rules appear without asking\n538: - **Hierarchy awareness** - Searches parent and sibling spec folders\n539: - **Entity linking** - Connects memories referencing the same concepts\n540: - **ANCHOR retrieval** - Per-section indexing (~93% token savings)\n541: - **Auto-surfacing** - Triggers on tool use and context compression events\n542: - **Provenance traces** - Shows exactly how each result was found\n543: \n544: &nbsp;\n545: #### Indexing and Infrastructure\n546: \n547: - **Real-time watching** - Filesystem monitoring via chokidar\n548: - **Incremental indexing** - Content hashes skip unchanged files\n549: - **Embedding retry** - Background worker retries failed embeddings\n550: - **Lexical fallback** - Text-searchable when embedding services are down\n551: - **Atomic writes** - Crash-safe with pending-file recovery on startup\n552: \n553: &nbsp;\n554: #### Evaluation\n555: \n556: - **12-metric computation** - MRR, NDCG, MAP and more\n557: - **Ground truth corpus** - 110 test questions with known correct answers\n558: - **Ablation studies** - Per-channel quality impact measurement\n559: - **Offline scoring checks** - Test ranking changes before deployment\n560: \n561: &nbsp;\n562: #### Embedding Providers\n563: \n564: The embedder layer is pluggable. Swap defaults via env vars without touching code. Canonical narrative: [embedder-pluggability.md](.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/references/embedder-pluggability.md).\n565: \n566: - **Ollama (nomic-embed-text-v1.5)** - Default since 2026-05-19 (ADR-013/014). Free, local, 768d retrieval-tuned. Pull once with `ollama pull nomic-embed-text:v1.5`. The cascade falls back to `jina-embeddings-v3` (1024d Q4_K_M) when nomic isn't pulled.\n567: - **HuggingFace Local** - Fallback when the Ollama probe fails. Free, local, 768d q8 ONNX.\n568: - **Voyage AI** - Cloud opt-in. Set `VOYAGE_API_KEY`. 1024d. Gated by egress guard.\n569: - **OpenAI** - Cloud opt-in. Set `OPENAI_API_KEY`. 1536d.\n570: \n571: ---\n572: \n573: ### ­¤öŹ CocoIndex + Code Graph\n574: \n575: The framework uses two different code-understanding systems on purpose. **CocoIndex** handles semantic discovery, so the assistant can answer \"find code that does X\" or \"how is Y implemented?\" without knowing exact symbols first. The **Code Graph** handles structural expansion, so the assistant can answer questions like \"what calls this?\", \"what imports this?\" or \"what breaks if we change it?\" using an indexed relationship graph.\n576: \n577: The intended routing order is graph-first: the code graph resolves structural queries first, CocoIndex finds semantic candidates when structural resolution misses and Memory supports session decisions and active-task context after the packet-local recovery sources have been checked. A 3-tier FTS fallback escalates automatically when results are weak.\n578: \n579: &nbsp;\n580: #### Default Scope (End-User Code Only)\n581: \n582: By default, code-graph scans your repo code only. Five `.opencode/` folders are excluded so end-user search results stay signal-rich:\n583: \n584: - `.opencode/skills/**`\n585: - `.opencode/agents/**`\n586: - `.opencode/commands/**`\n587: - `<active-spec-folder>/**`\n588: - `.opencode/plugins/**`\n589: \n590: Maintainers can opt folders back in process-wide with env vars:\n591: \n592: ```bash\n593: SPECKIT_CODE_GRAPH_INDEX_SKILLS=true       # all skills\n594: SPECKIT_CODE_GRAPH_INDEX_SKILLS=sk-x,sk-y  # only listed skills (csv)\n595: SPECKIT_CODE_GRAPH_INDEX_AGENTS=true\n596: SPECKIT_CODE_GRAPH_INDEX_COMMANDS=true\n597: SPECKIT_CODE_GRAPH_INDEX_SPECS=true\n598: SPECKIT_CODE_GRAPH_INDEX_PLUGINS=true\n599: SPECKIT_CODE_GRAPH_DB_DIR=/path/to/code-graph-db # optional DB-dir override\n600: ```\n601: \n602: Per-call args override env vars when provided. Env vars apply only for fields omitted from the scan call:\n603: \n604: ```ts\n605: code_graph_scan({\n606:   includeSkills: ['sk-code-review', 'sk-doc'], // granular: only these skills\n607:   includeAgents: true,                         // all .opencode/agents/**\n608: })\n609: ```\n610: \n611: Existing v1 scans trigger a blocked read with `requiredAction:\"code_graph_scan\"` until you re-run the scan. See [system-code-graph README ┬¦8 SCAN SCOPE](.opencode/skills/system-code-graph/README.md#8-scan-scope) for the full scan-scope rules and precedence details.\n612: \n613: Our CocoIndex is forked. The Python wrapper that powers semantic search is a soft-fork at version `0.2.3+spec-kit-fork.0.2.0`, vendored alongside the skill so it ships with this repo. The Rust engine underneath stays on PyPI. The fork adds four things the upstream wrapper doesn't: duplicate suppression so mirror copies of the same file don't crowd results, canonical path identity per chunk (so dedup works across symlinks), a path-class taxonomy that nudges \"find me the implementation of X\" toward implementation files first and ranking telemetry that surfaces *why* each result ranked where it did. Responses from the MCP tool or `ccc search` CLI carry seven fork-specific fields, `source_realpath`, `content_hash`, `path_class`, `dedupedAliases`, `uniqueResultCount`, `raw_score`, `rankingSignals`, that vanilla cocoindex output does not include. Schema, attribution and per-release patch list all live under [`.opencode/skills/mcp-coco-index/`](.opencode/skills/mcp-coco-index/).\n614: \n615: &nbsp;\n616: #### How the Code Graph Works\n617: \n618: The Code Graph is a SQLite-backed structural index owned by `.opencode/skills/system-code-graph/` and registered as the standalone `mk_code_index` MCP server. MCP callers use the `mcp__mk_code_index__*` namespace. Runtime config parity is mixed across clients during the rename transition, so docs use the canonical `mk_code_index` surface while follow-on config work handles remaining legacy bindings.\n619: \n620: **Startup injection.** When the MCP server starts, it initializes the `code-graph.sqlite` database, runs a non-blocking startup scan and activates a file watcher. Three supported runtimes (Claude Code, Gemini CLI, Codex CLI) transport the same compact startup shared-payload through their runtime hooks (`session-prime.ts` on Claude/Gemini, `session-start.ts` on Codex). Codex requires `[features].codex_hooks = true` opt-in for native hooks. Copilot CLI uses file-based custom instructions with a limited cache and writer path. It refreshes a managed block but does not inject model-visible context during the precompute phase. The payload includes a one-line health summary, `graphQualitySummary` (detector provenance + edge-enrichment summary) and the `sharedPayloadTransport` envelope so downstream consumers receive identical structural context regardless of runtime. `session_bootstrap()` remains available as a manual recovery surface when native hooks are disabled.\n621: \n622: **Auto-indexing.** The graph stays current through three mechanisms:\n623: 1. **Startup scan** - indexes on server boot (async, non-blocking)\n624: 2. **File watcher** - Chokidar monitors spec and source folders with a 2-second debounce, reindexing changed files in real time\n625: 3. **Lazy refresh** - `code_graph_query` calls `ensureCodeGraphReady()` which detects staleness and triggers a bounded inline refresh before returning results\n626: \n627: The indexer uses tree-sitter to parse source files and extract functions, classes, imports and call relationships. It tracks per-file content hashes to skip unchanged files, making incremental scans fast.\n628: \n629: &nbsp;\n630: #### Readiness & Response Contract\n631: \n632: `code_graph_query` and `code_graph_context` share a readiness-aware response contract. When the graph is fresh enough, both return `status: \"ok\"` with resolved results plus a `readiness` / `canonicalReadiness` / `trustState` block. When readiness requires a full scan that cannot run inline, both return an explicit **`status: \"blocked\"`** payload naming `requiredAction: \"code_graph_scan\"`, `blockReason: \"full_scan_required\"`, `degraded` and `graphAnswersOmitted` instead of silently returning empty results. Callers should run `code_graph_scan` before retrying.\n633: \n634: Success payloads of `code_graph_context` carry structured `data.metadata.partialOutput` (`isPartial`, `reasons`, `omittedSections`, `omittedAnchors`, `truncatedText`) and an explicit `deadlineMs` field so callers can distinguish a complete answer from one trimmed by deadline or budget pressure. `code_graph_status` exposes `graphQualitySummary` (detector provenance + edge-enrichment confidence). CALLS queries on ambiguous subjects (e.g. `handle*`) prefer callable implementation nodes over wrapper-shadow candidates and return ambiguity / selected-candidate metadata so callers can audit the choice.\n635: \n636: &nbsp;\n637: #### Edge Explanations and Better Blast Radius\n638: \n639: Relationship answers from `code_graph_query` include short `reason` and `step` fields alongside confidence and provenance, so you can see *why* an edge is there instead of just *that* it exists. `code_graph_context` carries those same fields through to structured edges and text briefs.\n640: \n641: `blast_radius` keeps the prior payload (affected files, source files, hot files, multi-file union, depth) and adds:\n642: \n643: - **`depthGroups`**: affected nodes bucketed by how far they sit from the change\n644: - **`riskLevel`**: `high` when the subject is ambiguous or fans out to more than 10 things at depth one, `medium` for 4ŌĆō10, `low` otherwise\n645: - **`minConfidence`** filter, drop traversals below a confidence floor\n646: - **`ambiguityCandidates`**: list of plausible matches when the subject can't be resolved\n647: - **`failureFallback`**: structured info instead of a bare error string when resolution can't continue\n648: \n649: All of this rides inside the existing `code_edges.metadata` JSON blob, no SQLite schema changes.\n650: \n651: &nbsp;\n652: #### `detect_changes`: Preflight Impact Check\n653: \n654: `detect_changes` is a read-only Code Graph tool that takes a diff and tells you which symbols and files it touches. It runs alongside `code_graph_scan`, `code_graph_query`, `code_graph_status` and `code_graph_context`.\n655: \n656: You hand it `{ diff: string, rootDir?: string }`. It walks each diff hunk, overlaps the line ranges with stored symbols and returns `{ status, affectedSymbols[], affectedFiles[], blockedReason?, timestamp, readiness }`.\n657: \n658: Safety is non-negotiable: the tool checks the graph is fresh before parsing the diff. If the graph is stale or unavailable, it returns `status: 'blocked'` immediately, so an out-of-date index never produces a false \"nothing impacted\" answer. Inline indexing is explicitly disabled here, so the read-only contract is enforced.\n659: \n660: Under the hood the scan runner is split into four declared phases (`find-candidates` ŌåÆ `parse-candidates` ŌåÆ `finalize` ŌåÆ `emit-metrics`) for clearer instrumentation, with no SQLite schema changes.\n661: \n662: The code graph runtime has its own feature catalog and operator playbook under [system-code-graph/feature_catalog](.opencode/skills/system-code-graph/feature_catalog/) and [system-code-graph/manual_testing_playbook](.opencode/skills/system-code-graph/manual_testing_playbook/). They document runtime features and manual scenarios for freshness, scan/verify/status, `detect_changes`, context retrieval, coverage graph, CCC and doctor-code-graph behavior.\n663: \n664: &nbsp;\n665: #### What Each System Does\n666: \n667: | System                   | Best for                                                                   | Primary surface                                                                  |\n668: | ------------------------ | -------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n669: | **CocoIndex**            | Concept search, similar implementations, unfamiliar modules                | `mcp__cocoindex_code__search`                                                    |\n670: | **Code Graph**           | Callers, imports, symbol outlines, impact analysis, neighborhood expansion | `mcp__mk_code_index__code_graph_*`, `mcp__mk_code_index__detect_changes`, `mcp__mk_code_index__ccc_*` |\n671: | **Session bridge tools** | Session bootstrap, resume and health checks around graph availability      | `session_bootstrap`, `session_resume`, `session_health`                          |\n672: | **CCC utilities**        | CocoIndex availability, reindexing, result feedback                        | `ccc_status`, `ccc_reindex`, `ccc_feedback`                                      |\n673: \n674: &nbsp;\n675: #### How Query Routing Works (Graph-First)\n676: \n677: The default routing order is: **Code Graph** (structural) -> **CocoIndex** (semantic code) -> **Memory** (session/decision context). This graph-first approach tries structural resolution before semantic similarity, with a 3-tier FTS fallback when earlier stages miss.\n678: \n679: - Use the **Code Graph** first for structural questions: callers, callees, imports, hierarchy, file outlines and reverse impact.\n680: - Use **CocoIndex** for semantic and intent-based questions: \"find code that validates memory quality\", \"show similar routing patterns\", \"where is the logic for X?\"\n681: - Use **session tools** when recovering or checking environment readiness, but treat `/spec_kit:resume` as the canonical operator-facing recovery surface.\n682: - Rebuild task continuity in this order: `handover.md` -> `_memory.continuity` -> canonical spec docs.\n683: - Use **Memory** after those packet-local sources when the question is about prior decisions, spec history, handovers or task continuity that still needs deeper retrieval.\n684: \n685: &nbsp;\n686: #### Why It Matters\n687: \n688: This split avoids forcing one search system to do everything poorly. Semantic search is good at resemblance. Structural search is good at relationships. Keeping both lets the framework move from \"this code looks relevant\" to \"this is how it connects\" without collapsing those concerns into a single noisy result set.\n689: \n690: For the full code-graph tool and architecture reference, see the [`system-code-graph` skill](.opencode/skills/system-code-graph/SKILL.md) and [system-code-graph README](.opencode/skills/system-code-graph/README.md). Shared memory and lifecycle details stay in [`.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/README.md`](.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/README.md).\n691: \n692: ---\n693: \n694: ### ­¤Ä» Skill Advisor\n695: \n696: The Skill Advisor matches what you type to the right skill before any tool runs. It is now a standalone MCP server named `mk_skill_advisor`, packaged under `.opencode/skills/system-skill-advisor/mcp_server/`. The server registers nine tools: eight on the public surface (four `advisor_*` tools for routing, freshness, rebuild and validation, plus four `skill_graph_*` tools for scan, query, status and graph validation), plus one internal propagation tool. A small Python compatibility shim still works as a fallback when the native path is unavailable.\n697: \n698: #### How It Works\n699: \n700: ```\n701:   YOU TYPE: \"use chrome-devtools to inspect a page\"\n702:                       Ōöé\n703:                       Ō¢╝\n704:            ŌöīŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöĆŌöÉ\n705:       1. The active set of detection markers and per-surface patterns lives inside `sk-code` ŌĆö see `.opencode/skills/sk-code/SKILL.md` ┬¦2 Smart Routing for the current detection list and `references/<surface>/` for per-surface conventions.\n10: \n11: **How It Works:** `sk-code` detects the active code surface from CWD/target paths and library markers, loads patterns from `.opencode/skills/sk-code/references/<surface>/`, and selects surface-appropriate verification (see Quick Reference). Surfaces it does not recognize trigger a disambiguation question rather than guessing.\n12: \n13: **The Iron Law:** NO completion claims without running stack-appropriate verification.\n14: \n15: ---\n16: \n17: ## 1. ­¤Ü© CRITICAL RULES\n18: \n19: ### Safety Constraints\n20: \n21: **HARD BLOCKERS (The \"Four Laws\" of Agent Safety):**\n22: 1. **READ FIRST:** Never edit a file without reading it first. Understand context before modifying.\n23: 2. **SCOPE LOCK:** Only modify files explicitly in scope. **NO** \"cleaning up\" or \"improving\" adjacent code. Scope in `spec.md` is FROZEN.\n24: 3. **VERIFY:** Syntax checks and tests **MUST** pass before claiming completion. **NO** blind commits.\n25: 4. **HALT:** Stop immediately if uncertain, if line numbers don't match, or if tests fail.\n26: \n27: **HALT CONDITIONS (Stop and Report):**\n28: - [ ] Target file does not exist or line numbers don't match.\n29: - [ ] Syntax check or Tests fail after edit.\n30: - [ ] Merge conflicts encountered.\n31: - [ ] Edit tool reports \"string not found\".\n32: - [ ] Test/Production boundary is unclear.\n33: \n34: **OPERATIONAL MANDATES:**\n35: - **All file modifications require a spec folder** (Gate 3).\n36: - **Never lie or fabricate** - use \"UNKNOWN\" when uncertain.\n37: - **Clarify** if confidence < 80% (see ┬¦4 Confidence Framework).\n38: - **Use explicit uncertainty:** Prefix claims with \"I'M UNCERTAIN ABOUT THIS:\".\n39: - **CLI dispatch rule** ŌĆö Before composing any prompt for `cli-X` (devin / codex / claude-code / gemini / opencode), you MUST `Read` `.opencode/skills/cli-X/SKILL.md` first. Advisor confidence Ōēź 0.8 does NOT waive this. Skills carry model-specific prompt-quality contracts (e.g. SWE-1.6's RCAF + medium-density pre-planning rule) that are not in the binary's `--help` and easy to miss. Any `<binary> --model <X>` invocation for a CLI with a `cli-X` skill requires the skill file in context.\n40: - **Small-model dispatch rule** ŌĆö Before dispatching to small models (SWE-1.6, DeepSeek-v4-pro, Kimi-k2.6, Qwen3.6, GLM-5.1 via cli-devin and/or cli-opencode; optional Haiku/Gemini Flash), you MUST consult `sk-ai-small-model` for pointers to context-budget defaults, output-verification recipes, model-profile registry, and structured-permissions schema. The sentinel skill is the single discoverable home for small-model optimization patterns and the canonical dispatch matrix (executor + provider + quota_pool per model). Routing is automatic via the advisor's `enhances` edges from cli-devin and cli-opencode, but the rule is here for explicit verification when sk-ai-small-model doesn't auto-surface.\n41: \n42: ---\n43: \n44: ### Request Analysis & Execution\n45: \n46: **Flow:** Parse request ŌåÆ Read files first ŌåÆ Analyze ŌåÆ Design simplest solution ŌåÆ Validate ŌåÆ Execute\n47: \n48: #### Execution Behavior\n49: \n50: - **Plan before acting** on multi-step work. Decide which files to read first, which tools to use, and how the result will be verified before making changes.\n51: - **Use a research-first approach.** Read the actual code, docs, and local instructions first. Never use an edit-first approach, and prefer surgical edits over broad rewrites.\n52: - **Apply project-specific conventions from `AGENTS.md`** before acting.\n53: - **Take responsibility for issues encountered during execution.** Do not dodge ownership with phrases like `not caused by my changes` or `pre-existing issue`; work toward the fix.\n54: - **Do not stop early when the requested solution is still incomplete.** Do not frame partial progress as a `good stopping point`, `natural checkpoint`, or `future work` when a safe path forward exists.\n55: - **Do not ask for permission to continue when the next safe step is already clear and in scope.** Avoid `should I continue?` or `want me to keep going?` when you can proceed safely under the existing rules.\n56: - **Use frequent self-checks and reasoning loops** to catch and fix your own mistakes before asking for help.\n57: - **Reason from actual data, not assumptions.** Verify against the real files, outputs, and behavior in front of you.\n58: \n59: \n60: ---\n61: \n62: ### Required Tools & Search Routing\n63: \n64: **MANDATORY TOOLS:**\n65: - **Spec Kit Memory MCP** - research, context recovery, saves. See Memory Save Rule below for save mechanics.\n66: - **CocoIndex Code MCP** - semantic code search. MUST use when exploring unfamiliar code, finding implementations by concept/intent, or when Grep/Glob exact matching is insufficient. Skill: `.opencode/skills/mcp-coco-index/`\n67: - **Git (sk-git)** - worktree setup, conventional commits, PR creation. Full details: `.opencode/skills/sk-git/`. Trigger keywords: worktree, branch, commit, merge, pr, pull request, git workflow, finish work, integrate changes\n68: \n69: **CODE SEARCH DECISION TREE:**\n70: \n71: ```text\n72: Need to find code?\n73:   |\n74:   +-- Know the exact text/token/symbol?\n75:   |     YES --> Grep (exact match)\n76:   |\n77:   +-- Know the file name or path?\n78:   |     YES --> Glob (pattern match)\n79:   |\n80:   +-- Searching by concept, intent, or \"how does X work\"?\n81:   |     YES --> CocoIndex search (semantic)\n82:   |             +-- Verify hits with Read\n83:   |             +-- Confirm with Grep if needed\n84:   |\n85:   +-- Exploring unfamiliar code?\n86:         YES --> CocoIndex search FIRST, then Grep/Glob to fill gaps\n87: ```\n88: \n89: CocoIndex triggers: \"find code that does X\", \"how is X implemented\", \"where is the logic for X\", \"similar code\", \"find patterns\", exploring unfamiliar modules, any intent-based query where exact tokens are unknown.\n90: \n91: | Approach     | Command                                                       | When                 |\n92: | ------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------- |\n93: | **MCP tool** | `search(query, languages, paths, num_results, refresh_index)` | AI agent integration |\n94: | **CLI**      | `ccc search \"query\" --lang X --path Y --limit N`              | Direct terminal use  |\n95: \n96: Set `refresh_index=false` after the first search in a session unless the codebase changed.\n97: \n98: ---\n99: \n100: ### Startup & Resume Recovery\n101: \n102: Hook-capable runtimes (Claude, Codex, Gemini, OpenCode) may inject startup context when wired. Per-runtime triggers: `.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/references/config/hook_system.md`. Feature-flag defaults: `.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/ENV_REFERENCE.md` (\"Feature flags reference table\").\n103: \n104: **Recovery flow when hooks are unavailable or fail:**\n105: \n106: 1. `/spec_kit:resume` is the canonical surface; rebuild context in order: `handover.md` ŌåÆ `_memory.continuity` ŌåÆ canonical spec docs (`implementation-summary.md` ŌåÆ `tasks.md` ŌåÆ `plan.md` ŌåÆ `spec.md`).\n107: 2. **Phase parent** (target has `[0-9]{3}-name/` children with their own spec/description): honor `graph-metadata.json.derived.last_active_child_id`, else list children with statuses. Lean trio policy ŌĆö only `spec.md`, `description.json`, `graph-metadata.json` live at parent; read the chosen child's continuity ladder, NOT the parent's plan/tasks/implementation-summary.\n108: 3. Stale or missing structural context: run `session_bootstrap()`, then `code_graph_scan` if needed. Graph unavailable: use CocoIndex + direct reads, but keep the packet-local continuity ladder as source-of-truth. Code-graph implementation/docs are owned by `.opencode/skills/system-code-graph/`; tool names stay stable.\n109: 4. Re-anchor on spec folder, current task, blockers, and next steps before making changes.\n110: \n111: ---\n112: \n113: ### Quality & Anti-Patterns\n114: \n115: **QUALITY PRINCIPLES:**\n116: - **Prefer simplicity**, reuse existing patterns, and cite evidence with sources\n117: - Solve only the stated problem; **avoid over-engineering** and premature optimization\n118: - **Verify with checks** (simplicity, performance, maintainability, scope) before making changes\n119: - **Truth over agreement** - correct user misconceptions with evidence; do not agree for conversational flow\n120: \n121: **ANTI-PATTERNS (Detect Silently):**\n122: \n123: | Anti-Pattern           | Trigger Phrases                                 | Response                                                                    |\n124: | ---------------------- | ----------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n125: | Over-engineering       | \"for flexibility\", \"future-proof\", \"might need\" | Ask: \"Is this solving a current problem or a hypothetical one?\"             |\n126: | Premature optimization | \"could be slow\", \"might bottleneck\"             | Ask: \"Has this been measured? What's the actual performance?\"               |\n127: | Cargo culting          | \"best practice\", \"always should\"                | Ask: \"Does this pattern fit this specific case?\"                            |\n128: | Gold-plating           | \"while we're here\", \"might as well\"             | Flag scope creep: \"That's a separate change - shall I note it for later?\"   |\n129: | Wrong abstraction      | \"DRY this up\" for 2 instances                   | \"These look similar but might not be the same concept. Let's verify first.\" |\n130: | Scope creep            | \"also add\", \"bonus feature\"                     | \"That's outside the current scope. Want to track it separately?\"            |\n131: \n132: **ANALYSIS LENSES:**\n133: \n134: | Lens               | Focus            | Detection Questions                                                                |\n135: | ------------------ | ---------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n136: | **CLARITY**        | Simplicity       | Is this the simplest code that solves the problem? Are abstractions earned?        |\n137: | **SYSTEMS**        | Dependencies     | What does this change touch? What calls this? What are the side effects?           |\n138: | **BIAS**           | Wrong problem    | Is user solving a symptom? Is this premature optimization? Is the framing correct? |\n139: | **SUSTAINABILITY** | Maintainability  | Will future devs understand this? Is it self-documenting? Tech debt implications?  |\n140: | **VALUE**          | Actual impact    | Does this change behavior or just refactor? Is it cosmetic or functional?          |\n141: | **SCOPE**          | Complexity match | Does solution complexity match problem size? Single-line fix or new abstraction?   |\n142: \n143: ---\n144: \n145: ### Quick Reference: Common Workflows\n146: \n147: | Task                                 | Flow                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |\n148: | ------------------------------------ | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n149: | **Resume prior work**                | `/spec_kit:resume` ŌåÆ Rebuild context from `handover.md` ŌåÆ `_memory.continuity` ŌåÆ canonical spec docs ŌåÆ Review ŌåÆ Continue                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |\n150: | **New spec folder**                  | Option B (Gate 3) ŌåÆ Research via Task tool ŌåÆ Evidence-based plan ŌåÆ Approval ŌåÆ Implement                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |\n151: | **Code work**                        | sk-code skill ŌåÆ smart router (auto-detects the active stack from CWD + library markers; C) Cite user's explicit direction: \"User specified: [exact quote]\"\n190: - Confidence Ōēź 0.8 ŌåÆ MUST invoke skill | < 0.8 ŌåÆ general approach | User names skill ŌåÆ cite and proceed\n191: - Output: `SKILL ROUTING: [result]` or `SKILL ROUTING: User directed ŌåÆ [name]`\n192: - Skip: trivial queries only (greetings, single-line questions)\n193: \n194: #### GATE 3: SPEC FOLDER QUESTION [HARD] BLOCK - PRIORITY GATE\n195: - **Overrides Gates 1-2:** If file modification detected ŌåÆ ask Gate 3 BEFORE any analysis/tool calls\n196: - **Machine contract:** `.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/shared/gate-3-classifier.ts` (`classifyPrompt()`). The prose lists below are human-readable; the classifier module is authoritative for runtimes that call it.\n197: - **Positive triggers (write actions):** create, add, remove, delete, rename, move, update, change, modify, edit, fix, refactor, implement, build, write, generate, configure\n198: - **Positive triggers (continuity writes):** `save context`, `save memory`, `/memory:save`, `/spec_kit:resume`, `resume iteration`, `resume deep research`, `resume deep review`, `continue iteration` (these produce `description.json` / `graph-metadata.json` / continuity frontmatter / `iteration-NNN.md` writes)\n199: - **Read-only disqualifiers:** `review`, `audit`, `inspect`, `analyze`, `explain` ŌĆö suppress Gate 3 when they appear ALONE (e.g. \"review the decomposition phase\"). OVERVIEW](#1--overview)\n28: - [2. QUICK START](#2--quick-start)\n29: - [3. FEATURES](#3--features)\n30: - [4. STRUCTURE](#4--structure)\n31: - [5. CONFIGURATION](#5--configuration)\n32: - [6. OVERVIEW\n43: \n44: `.opencode/skills/` holds 19 skill folders. Skills are not passive references. Each skill contains executable guidance that an AI agent loads on demand through Gate 2 routing or explicit invocation. Skills carry their own references, assets, scripts, and graph metadata so domain knowledge stays close to the code that uses it.\n45: \n46: Skills divide into five categories: CLI orchestrators that delegate work to external AI binaries, MCP integrations that wrap third-party tools, code workflow and review skills, documentation and improvement-loop utilities, and the system packages that govern routing, code graph, and file-modifying workflows. The primary routing engine is now the native TypeScript Skill Advisor package at `system-skill-advisor/mcp_server/`, exposed through four `advisor_*` tools and four `skill_graph_*` tools. The Python `system-skill-advisor/mcp_server/scripts/skill_advisor.py` entrypoint remains as a compatibility shim with native-first delegation and local fallback.\n47: \n48: Adding a skill is intentional. Every new skill goes through `sk-doc`'s scaffolding workflow, gets a SKILL.md with proper frontmatter, and is discovered by the native advisor through graph metadata indexing. The Python shim can still discover it directly when fallback mode is active.\n49: \n50: ### Key Statistics\n51: \n52: | Metric | Value | Notes |\n53: | --- | --- | --- |\n54: | Total skill folders | 20 | Top-level non-hidden skills under `.opencode/skills/` |\n55: | Folders with graph metadata | 20 | Every top-level non-hidden skill folder under `.opencode/skills/` currently ships with `graph-metadata.json` |\n56: | Graph families | 6 | `cli`, `mcp`, `sk-code`, `sk-util`, `system`, `deep-loop` |\n57: | CLI orchestrator skills | 5 | cli-claude-code, cli-codex, cli-devin, cli-gemini, cli-opencode |\n58: | MCP integration skills | 3 | mcp-chrome-devtools, mcp-coco-index, mcp-code-mode |\n59: | Code workflow and review skills | 2 | sk-code, sk-code-review |\n60: | sk-util utility skills | 6 | deep-agent-improvement, sk-ai-council, sk-ai-small-model, sk-doc, sk-git, sk-prompt |\n61: | Deep-loop autonomous skills | 2 | deep-research, deep-review |\n62: | System skills | 4 | system-code-graph, system-rerank-sidecar, system-skill-advisor, system-spec-kit |\n63: | Skills with local scripts/ | 9 | See Section 4 for the current script-bearing folders |\n64: | Native advisor tools | 8 | `advisor_*` plus `skill_graph_*` tools exposed by `mk_skill_advisor` |\n65: | Shared compatibility scripts | 5 | `skill_advisor.py`, runtime, bench, regression, and graph compiler |\n66: \n67: ### Key Features\n68: \n69: | Feature | Description |\n70: | --- | --- |\n71: | Gate 2 routing | Native `advisor_recommend` scores requests with 5-lane fusion and returns prompt-safe recommendations |\n72: | Advisor health and validation | `advisor_status` reports freshness, `skillCount`, `lastScanAt`, and lane weights; `advisor_validate` returns measured corpus, holdout, parity, safety, and latency slices |\n73: | Graph metadata system | Per-folder `graph-metadata.json` feeds the SQLite skill graph, with `system-skill-advisor/mcp_server/scripts/skill-graph.json` kept for export and fallback workflows |\n74: | On-demand loading | Skills load only when needed so context stays focused |\n75: | Self-contained skills | References, assets, and scripts live inside each skill folder |\n76: | Auto-discovery | New skills are found through graph metadata and SKILL.md discovery |\n77: | Dual-threshold filtering | Confidence and uncertainty both gate routing to reduce false positives |\n78: \n79: <!-- /ANCHOR:overview -->\n80: \n81: ---\n82: \n83: <!-- ANCHOR:quick-start -->\n84: ## 2. QUICK START\n85: \n86: Three ways to use this library:\n87: \n88: **1. Route with Gate 2**\n89: \n90: Use the native advisor before any non-trivial task when MCP is available. Use the Python shim when a runtime needs the legacy JSON-array contract.\n91: \n92: ```text\n93: advisor_recommend({\"prompt\":\"rewrite README for skill library\",\"options\":{\"topK\":1}})\n94: ```\n95: \n96: ```bash\n97: python3 .opencode/skills/system-skill-advisor/mcp_server/scripts/skill_advisor.py \"rewrite README for skill library\" --threshold 0.8\n98: ```\n99: \n100: **2. Open a skill directly**\n101: \n102: Read the SKILL.md for any skill to load its instructions into context.\n103: \n104: ```bash\n105: # Read the first 120 lines (covers overview and routing sections)\n106: sed -n '1,120p' .opencode/skills/sk-doc/SKILL.md\n107: ```\n108: \n109: **3. Run skill-local scripts**\n110: \n111: Many skills ship their own scripts. Reference them by the skill's path.\n112: \n113: ```bash\n114: python3 .opencode/skills/sk-doc/scripts/validate_document.py README.md\n115: python3 .opencode/skills/sk-doc/scripts/extract_structure.py README.md --json\n116: ```\n117: \n118: Loading sequence:\n119: \n120: ```text\n121: Request -> advisor_recommend -> top match + confidence -> load SKILL.md -> follow instructions\n122: ```\n123: \n124: <!-- /ANCHOR:quick-start -->\n125: \n126: ---\n127: \n128: <!-- ANCHOR:features -->\n129: ## 3. FEATURES\n130: \n131: ### 3.1 FEATURE HIGHLIGHTS\n132: \n133: The skill system covers four distinct workflow domains.\n134: \n135: **CLI Delegation.** The five CLI skills (cli-claude-code, cli-codex, cli-devin, cli-gemini, cli-opencode) let any AI assistant hand off work to an external AI binary. Each skill specifies the right binary flags, model selection, prompt formatting, and output parsing. This enables parallel execution and cross-AI validation without the calling AI needing to know binary internals. cli-devin uniquely adds local-to-cloud handoff for async multi-hour work.\n136: \n137: **MCP Tool Wrapping.** The three MCP integration skills route tool calls through Code Mode or package-local MCP surfaces for token-efficient execution. mcp-code-mode is the hub for external services, mcp-chrome-devtools handles browser debugging, and mcp-coco-index adds semantic code search via vector embeddings for finding relevant implementations by concept rather than exact keyword.\n138: \n139: **Code Workflow Skills.** `sk-code` provides **multi-stack coding standards, references, and assets** ŌĆö surface-aware patterns, checklists, and verification recipes for project-specific frontend and system-code surfaces (JavaScript, TypeScript, Python, Shell, JSON/JSONC, MCP/agents/commands/skills). Smart-routing internals auto-detect the active stack. `sk-code-review` provides the findings-first review baseline and uses `sk-code` surface evidence where applicable.\n140: \n141: **System Foundation.** system-spec-kit governs all file modifications through spec folder workflows (Levels 1-3+), template validation, and Spec Kit Memory for context preservation across sessions. system-skill-advisor owns Gate 2 routing and the skill graph, while system-code-graph owns the `mk-code-index` structural graph MCP tools. system-spec-kit remains mandatory for every task involving file changes.\n142: \n143: ### 3.2 FEATURE REFERENCE\n144: \n145: **CLI Orchestrator Skills**\n146: \n147: | Skill | Version | Description |\n148: | --- | --- | --- |\n149: | `cli-claude-code` | 1.1.1 | Invokes Claude Code CLI for deep reasoning, code editing, structured output, and agent delegation |\n150: | `cli-codex` | 1.3.1 | Invokes OpenAI Codex CLI for code generation, review, web research, and parallel task processing |\n151: | `cli-devin` | 1.0.0 | Invokes Cognition's Devin CLI for autonomous coding (SWE-1.6 default + DeepSeek v4 / GLM 5.1 / Kimi k2.6 for complex work) plus local-to-cloud handoff |\n152: | `cli-gemini` | 1.2.1 | Invokes Google Gemini CLI for code generation, Google Search grounding, and architecture analysis |\n153: | `cli-opencode` | 1.0.0 | Invokes OpenCode CLI for full plugin/skill/MCP runtime dispatch, parallel detached sessions, and cross-AI orchestration |\n154: \n155: **MCP Integration Skills**\n156: \n157: | Skill | Version | Description |\n158: | --- | --- | --- |\n159: | `mcp-chrome-devtools` | 1.0.7.0 | Browser debugging via CLI (bdg) with MCP fallback for multi-tool integration |\n160: | `mcp-coco-index` | 1.0.0 | Semantic code search via vector embeddings using natural-language queries |\n161: | `mcp-code-mode` | 1.0.7.0 | TypeScript-based MCP orchestration hub for all external tool calls |\n162: \n163: **Code Quality Skills**\n164: \n165: | Skill | Version | Description |\n166: | --- | --- | --- |\n167: | `sk-code` | 1.1.0.0 | Multi-stack coding standards, references, and assets (project-specific frontend and system-code surfaces) |\n168: | `sk-code-review` | 1.2.0.0 | Findings-first code review baseline with security and correctness minimums |\n169: \n170: **Documentation, Research, Prompt, and Improvement Skills**\n171: \n172: | Skill | Version | Description |\n173: | --- | --- | --- |\n174: | `deep-agent-improvement` | 1.0.0.0 | Evaluator-first agent improvement with 5-dimension integration-aware scoring, dynamic profiling, deterministic benchmarks, and guarded promotion |\n175: | `sk-ai-council` | 1.0.0.0 | Multi-seat planning council for complex scoped-write decisions and convergence artifacts |\n176: | `deep-research` | 1.2.0 | Autonomous research loop with iterative investigation, externalized state, and convergence detection |\n177: | `deep-review` | 1.0.0 | Autonomous iterative code review with severity-weighted findings, dimension coverage, convergence detection, and release readiness verdicts |\n178: | `sk-doc` | 1.3.0.0 | Markdown quality enforcement, component templates, validation scripts, and DQI scoring |\n179: | `sk-prompt` | 1.2.0.0 | Prompt engineering using 7 frameworks (RCAF, COSTAR, RACE, CIDI, TIDD-EC, CRISPE, CRAFT) |\n180: \n181: **Git and System Skills**\n182: \n183: | Skill | Version | Description |\n184: | --- | --- | --- |\n185: | `sk-git` | 1.1.0.0 | Git workflow orchestrator for workspace setup, clean commits, and work completion |\n186: | `system-code-graph` | 1.0.0.0 | Structural code indexing and `mk-code-index` MCP workflows |\n187: | `system-skill-advisor` | 0.1.0 | Standalone Gate 2 routing package and skill graph MCP server |\n188: | `system-spec-kit` | 2.2.27.0 | Spec folder workflow, template architecture, validation, and Spec Kit Memory |\n189: \n190: <!-- /ANCHOR:features -->\n191: \n192: ---\n193: \n194: <!-- ANCHOR:structure -->\n195: ## 4.
