Agent counterpart listed in the Agent Network section below\n940: \n941: ---\n942: \n943: ### ­¤ż¢ Agent Network\n944: \n945: 11 custom specialist agents. Defined in `.opencode/agents/` (source of truth), mirrored for Claude Code (`.claude/agents/`), Codex CLI (`.codex/agents/`) and Gemini CLI (`.gemini/agents/`) runtime surfaces. OpenCode and Copilot CLI use runtime-specific MCP and startup integration rather than a dedicated agent mirror.\n946: \n947: **Orchestrate**\n948: - Senior task commander with full authority over decomposition, delegation and quality evaluation\n949: - Merges sub-agent outputs into one unified response with conflict resolution\n950: - Read-only permissions - delegates implementation to other agents\n951: - Single-hop delegation only (depth 2 max) to prevent runaway chains\n952: \n953: **Code**\n954: - Surface-aware code implementation specialist (write-capable LEAF, `mode: subagent`, `task: deny`)\n955: - Delegates code surface detection to `sk-code`. The agent body itself stays stack-agnostic and reads sk-code's emitted surface evidence at dispatch time\n956: - 7 dispatch modes: full implementation / surgical fix / refactor only / test add / scaffold new file / rename-move / dependency bump\n957: - 5-dimension acceptance rubric (100 pts total): Correctness 30, Scope-Adherence 20, Verification-Evidence 20, Stack-Pattern-Compliance 15, Integration 15\n958: - Builder ŌåÆ Critic ŌåÆ Verifier adversarial self-check on every completion claim (challenges `DONE`, opposite axis from `@review`'s Hunter/Skeptic/Referee which challenges findings)\n959: - Iron Law: NO COMPLETION CLAIMS WITHOUT FRESH VERIFICATION EVIDENCE FROM THE ACTUAL STACK. LOW confidence strictly blocks `DONE`\n960: - Fail-closed verification, failure returns to orchestrator, no internal retry. BLOCKED-count circuit breaker (3├Ś BLOCKED ŌåÆ orchestrator offers `@debug`)\n961: - Compact RETURN line + structured body with `escalation` classifier (NONE / UNKNOWN_STACK / SCOPE_CONFLICT / LOW_CONFIDENCE / LOGIC_SYNC / VERIFY_FAIL)\n962: - Dispatched ONLY by `@orchestrate` via convention-floor caller-restriction (description prose + body ┬¦0 dispatch gate + orchestrate.md routing entry. Not harness-enforced)\n963: \n964: **Context**\n965: - Memory-first retrieval specialist - always checks memory before codebase\n966: - Search order: `match_triggers` ŌåÆ `memory_context` ŌåÆ `memory_search` ŌåÆ grep/glob\n967: - Returns structured Context Packages combining memory findings with codebase evidence\n968: - Uses both CocoIndex semantic search and the 5-channel memory system. Read-only.\n969: \n970: **Review**\n971: - Code quality guardian with strict read-only permissions (cannot write or edit any file)\n972: - Loads `sk-code-review` baseline first, then uses `sk-code` surface evidence for stack-specific standards (whatever surface `sk-code` detected)\n973: - Security and correctness minimums are mandatory and never relaxed by surface-specific evidence\n974: - Produces findings-first severity analysis with quality scoring and pattern validation\n975: \n976: **Debug**\n977: - Fresh-perspective debugger that receives structured context handoff (not conversation history)\n978: - Avoids inherited bias from failed prior attempts - use after 3+ failed debugging tries\n979: - Systematic 5-phase methodology: Observe ŌåÆ Analyze ŌåÆ Hypothesize ŌåÆ Validate ŌåÆ Fix\n980: - Writes `debug-delegation.md` with root cause analysis and findings\n981: \n982: **Markdown**\n983: - Dedicated LEAF executor for the `/create:*` command family (agent, sk-skill, feature-catalog, testing-playbook, folder_readme, changelog) plus scoped spec-doc and markdown authoring\n984: - Scope-gated by convention-level Phase 0 check. Refuses unscoped writes and nested delegation with canonical REFUSE wording\n985: - Loads `sk-doc` skill on every invocation. Reads the per-command or document-appropriate template before writing\n986: - Deterministic 3-state output contract: `STATUS=OK PATH=<file>` / `STATUS=FAIL ERROR=<reason>` / `STATUS=CANCELLED`\n987: - DQI score >=75 minimum reported in completion claim. HVR (Human Voice Rules) compliance enforced\n988: \n989: **Prompt-Improver**\n990: - Prompt-escalation specialist for high-stakes external CLI invocations and other sensitive AI prompt work\n991: - Selects the best-fit framework from `sk-prompt`, applies DEPTH at the right energy level and validates the result with CLEAR\n992: - Returns a structured prompt package with `FRAMEWORK`, `CLEAR_SCORE`, `RATIONALE`, `ENHANCED_PROMPT` and `ESCALATION_NOTES`\n993: - Used by the CLI mirror-card pipeline and `/improve:prompt` agent mode when complexity, compliance or stakeholder spread makes inline prompting too weak\n994: \n995: **Deep AI Council**\n996: - Multi-strategy planning architect dispatching diverse AI vantage points and strategy lenses\n997: - Seeks distinct reasoning strategies across multiple AIs (cli-codex, cli-gemini, cli-claude-code + native)\n998: - Multi-round deliberation before recommending a plan. Planning-only (never modifies files)\n999: - 5-dimension scoring rubric for strategy quality\n1000: \n1001: **Deep Research**\n1002: - Autonomous research agent executing single LEAF (Loop, Externalize, Analyze, Finish) iterations\n1003: - State externalized via JSONL + strategy.md for pause/resume across sessions\n1004: - Loop orchestration managed by `/deep:start-research-loop` command, not this agent\n1005: - Has permission to write `research.md` and `scratch/` inside spec folders\n1006: - 3-signal convergence model: Rolling Average (0.45), MAD Noise Floor (0.30), Coverage/Age (0.25) with 0.60 threshold\n1007: - Semantic coverage graph: each iteration emits `graphEvents` with relation types (ANSWERS, SUPPORTS, CONTRADICTS, SUPERSEDES, DERIVED_FROM, COVERS, CITES)\n1008: - Graph convergence guards: sourceDiversity (>= 0.4) and evidenceDepth (>= 1.5) block premature STOP\n1009: - Question coverage tracking computes answerCoverage ratio from ANSWERS edges\n1010: - Quality guards: source diversity, focus alignment and weak-source checks must pass before STOP\n1011: - Progressive synthesis: `research.md` updated incrementally and finalized during synthesis\n1012: - Negative knowledge: ruled-out directions and dead ends preserved as first-class outputs\n1013: - Lifecycle modes: `new`, `resume`, `restart` (fork and completed-continue are deferred)\n1014: - Fail-closed corruption handling: throws structured error before writing derived files when JSONL is corrupt\n1015: - Graph convergence fallback: scoring uses a numeric fallback when `blendedScore` is absent\n1016: \n1017: **Deep Review**\n1018: - Autonomous code quality auditor using LEAF architecture for single review iterations\n1019: - Reviews code but NEVER modifies target files (read-only on code)\n1020: - Loop orchestration managed by `/deep:start-review-loop` command, not this agent\n1021: - Produces P0/P1/P2 severity-ranked findings with `file:line` evidence across 4 review dimensions (Correctness, Security, Traceability, Maintainability)\n1022: - Severity-weighted convergence: P0 contributes weight 10.0, P1 contributes 5.0, P2 contributes 1.0. Refinements contribute 0.5x those weights\n1023: - 3-signal convergence model: Rolling Average (0.45), MAD Noise Floor (0.30), Dimension Coverage (0.25)\n1024: - P0 override: any new P0 finding forces at least one more iteration regardless of convergence math\n1025: - Adversarial self-check on P0 findings: Hunter/Skeptic/Referee triad before admission\n1026: - Binary quality gates: evidence (file:line backed), scope (stays inside declared target), coverage (all dimensions and cross-reference protocols complete)\n1027: - Graph-aware legal-stop checks using structural graph signals from `graphEvents`\n1028: - Semantic coverage graph with review-specific node types (DIMENSION, FILE, FINDING, EVIDENCE, REMEDIATION) and edge types (COVERS, EVIDENCE_FOR, IN_DIMENSION, CONTRADICTS, RESOLVES, CONFIRMS)\n1029: - 9-section review report with PASS/CONDITIONAL/FAIL verdict (FAIL on P0, CONDITIONAL on P1, PASS otherwise)\n1030: - Claim-adjudication `finalSeverity` overrides original severity in the findings registry\n1031: - Fail-closed corruption handling: reducer refuses to write derived files when JSONL corruption is detected\n1032: - Lifecycle modes: `new`, `resume`, `restart` with typed JSONL lineage events\n1033: \n1034: **Agent Improver**\n1035: - Proposal-only mutator for bounded agent improvement experiments\n1036: - Reads the target agent's charter, manifest and integration surface, then writes ONE candidate to a packet-local runtime area\n1037: - Never scores, promotes, benchmarks or edits canonical targets. The `/improve:agent` command loop handles those.\n1038: - Loop orchestration: scan integration surfaces, generate dynamic profile, dispatch this agent, score candidate across 5 dimensions (structural, ruleCoherence, integration, outputQuality, systemFitness), reduce state, check stop conditions\n1039: \n1040: ---\n1041: \n1042: ### Ōī©’ĖÅ Commands\n1043: \n1044: 22 command entry points across 6 namespaces. Each command is a Markdown entry point under `.opencode/commands/**/*.md` backed by a behavioral execution spec.\n1045: \n1046: &nbsp;\n1047: #### SPEC KIT\n1048: \n1049: **Plan --intake-only**\n1050: - Standalone intake workflow that publishes `spec.md`, `description.json` and `graph-metadata.json`\n1051: - Used directly for new packet setup and paired with `/spec_kit:plan` or `/spec_kit:complete` when `folder_state` is `no-spec`, `partial-folder`, `repair-mode` or `placeholder-upgrade`\n1052: - Modes: `:auto`, `:confirm`\n1053: \n1054: **Complete**\n1055: - End-to-end workflow: intake/delegate ŌåÆ research ŌåÆ plan ŌåÆ implement ŌåÆ verify ŌåÆ save memory\n1056: - Smart-detects missing or unhealthy packet state and reuses the shared intake contract from `/spec_kit:plan --intake-only`. Healthy folders continue without extra setup prompts\n1057: - Modes: `:auto` (fully autonomous), `:confirm` (pause at each step), `:with-research` (adds deep research)\n1058: - After 3 failed implementation attempts, surface diagnostics and let the user dispatch `@debug` via the Task tool\n1059: \n1060: **Plan**\n1061: - Planning-only workflow that authors `spec.md`, `plan.md` and `tasks.md` without implementing\n1062: - Reuses the shared intake contract from `/spec_kit:plan --intake-only` when the packet is `no-spec`, `partial-folder`, `repair-mode` or `placeholder-upgrade`\n1063: - Dispatches up to 4 parallel context agents for codebase exploration during planning\n1064: - Use when you need stakeholder review before coding. Modes: `:auto`, `:confirm`\n1065: \n1066: **Implement**\n1067: - Executes an existing plan - requires plan.md to already exist\n1068: - 9-step workflow covering task breakdown, implementation, testing and verification\n1069: - Modes: `:auto`, `:confirm`\n1070: \n1071: **Debug**\n1072: - Delegates debugging to the debug agent with structured context handoff (not conversation history)\n1073: - Fresh-perspective approach avoids confirmation bias from failed prior attempts\n1074: - Writes `debug-delegation.md` with root cause analysis\n1075: \n1076: **Resume**\n1077: - Continues a previous session by auto-loading memory from the spec folder\n1078: - Presents session summary, shows progress against tasks.md\n1079: - Works after crashes, compactions or new sessions\n1080: \n1081: **Deep Research**\n1082: - Autonomous research loop dispatching deep-research agents iteratively until convergence\n1083: - Anchors every run to a real `spec.md` under `spec_check_protocol.md`, with advisory lock handling, `folder_state` detection and bounded `BEGIN/END GENERATED` write-back\n1084: - Externalized JSONL state enables pause/resume across sessions\n1085: - Reducer parses terminal `synthesis_complete` events for authoritative stop metadata\n1086: - Graph convergence guards block premature STOP when sourceDiversity or evidenceDepth thresholds fail\n1087: - Lifecycle modes: `new`, `resume`, `restart` with lineage tracking across generations\n1088: - Modes: `:auto`, `:confirm`\n1089: \n1090: **Deep Review**\n1091: - Autonomous code review loop dispatching deep-review agents iteratively until convergence\n1092: - Severity-weighted findings (P0/P1/P2) across 4 dimensions with release readiness verdicts (PASS/CONDITIONAL/FAIL)\n1093: - Claim-adjudication packets with `finalSeverity` override, stale STOP veto auto-clearing\n1094: - Binary quality gates (evidence, scope, coverage) checked after convergence math before allowing stop\n1095: - Adversarial self-check on P0 findings using Hunter/Skeptic/Referee triad\n1096: - Lifecycle modes: `new`, `resume`, `restart` with typed JSONL lineage events\n1097: - Modes: `:auto`, `:confirm`\n1098: \n1099: **Handover**\n1100: - Creates session handover document for continuing work in a new conversation\n1101: - Gathers key decisions, blockers, current phase and next steps from spec folder state\n1102: - Variants: `:quick` (summary) or `:full` (comprehensive)\n1103: \n1104: **Spec-first command chains**\n1105: \n1106: ```text\n1107: /spec_kit:plan --intake-only\n1108:   Ōö£ŌöĆŌ¢║ /spec_kit:plan -> /spec_kit:implement\n1109:   Ōö£ŌöĆŌ¢║ /deep:start-research-loop -> /spec_kit:plan\n1110:   ŌööŌöĆŌ¢║ /spec_kit:complete\n1111:        ŌööŌöĆŌ¢║ reuses the shared intake contract from /spec_kit:plan --intake-only when folder_state still needs intake\n1112: ```\n1113: \n1114: `/deep:start-research-loop` only enters that chain after a real `spec.md` exists. It follows `spec_check_protocol.md` for advisory-lock handling, `folder_state` classification and bounded generated-fence sync.\n1115: \n1116: &nbsp;\n1117: #### MEMORY\n1118: \n1119: **Save**\n1120: - Updates packet continuity and supporting generated context artifacts via `generate-context.js`\n1121: - AI composes structured JSON with session summary, key decisions and findings\n1122: - Indexes immediately for future retrieval via `memory_save()` or `memory_index_scan()`\n1123: \n1124: **Search**\n1125: - Unified retrieval and analysis entry point with intent-aware routing\n1126: - Supports epistemic baselines, causal graph traversal, ablation studies and dashboards\n1127: - Routes by intent: `add_feature`, `fix_bug`, `refactor`, `security_audit`, `understand`, `find_spec`, `find_decision`\n1128: \n1129: **Learn**\n1130: - `/memory:learn` constitutional memory manager for always-surface rules\n1131: - Constitutional memories carry a 3.0x boost and never decay\n1132: - Lifecycle operations: create, list, edit, remove, budget\n1133: \n1134: **Manage**\n1135: - Database admin: stats (memory counts, index health), health checks, cleanup (orphaned vectors)\n1136: - Checkpoint management: create, list, restore, delete\n1137: - Bulk operations and ingestion (start/status/cancel)\n1138: \n1139: &nbsp;\n1140: #### CREATE\n1141: \n1142: **Skill**\n1143: - Unified skill creation and update workflow\n1144: - Creates SKILL.md with 8-section structure, README.md, references and assets directories\n1145: - Registers in skill catalog. Modes: `:auto`, `:confirm`\n1146: \n1147: **Agent**\n1148: - Scaffolds a new agent definition with proper frontmatter, behavioral rules and tool permissions\n1149: - Creates source-of-truth file in `.opencode/agents/` and mirrors for Claude, Codex, Gemini runtimes\n1150: - Modes: `:auto`, `:confirm`\n1151: \n1152: **Readme**\n1153: - Unified README and install guide creation using sk-doc quality standards\n1154: - Auto-detects folder type, loads appropriate template, validates via DQI scoring\n1155: - Structure 40%, Content 35%, Style 25%. Modes: `:auto`, `:confirm`\n1156: \n1157: **Changelog**\n1158: - Auto-detects recent work from spec folder artifacts or git history\n1159: - Resolves correct component folder, calculates next version number\n1160: - Generates formatted changelog file matching 370+ existing entries. Modes: `:auto`, `:confirm`\n1161: \n1162: **Prompt (planned)**\n1163: - `/create:prompt` is a reserved surface, but there is no shipped `.opencode/commands/create/prompt.md` entry point in this repo snapshot\n1164: - Use `/improve:prompt` or the `sk-prompt` skill directly when you need prompt work today\n1165: \n1166: **Feature Catalog**\n1167: - Creates or updates feature catalog packages with category routing\n1168: - Generates both technical reference entries and simple-terms companion entries\n1169: - Validates against the 290-entry catalog structure across 22 categories\n1170: \n1171: **Testing Playbook**\n1172: - Creates or updates manual testing playbook packages\n1173: - Generates scenario files with test steps, expected results and verification evidence fields\n1174: - Validates against established playbook format\n1175: \n1176: The MCP server also ships explicit stress and matrix execution surfaces. Run `npm run stress` from [mcp_server/](.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/) for the dedicated [stress_test/](.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/stress_test/) suite, which covers search-quality, memory, skill-advisor, code-graph, session and matrix subsystems. [matrix_runners/](.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/matrix_runners/) provides four per-CLI adapters plus a manifest and meta-runner for the F1-F14 feature matrix across `cli-codex`, `cli-gemini`, `cli-claude-code` and `cli-opencode`.\n1177: \n1178: &nbsp;\n1179: #### IMPROVE\n1180: \n1181: **Improve Agent**\n1182: - Evaluates and improves any agent across 5 integration-aware dimensions with deterministic scoring\n1183: - Runs a bounded loop: scan integration surfaces, generate dynamic profile, dispatch `@deep-agent-improvement`, score candidate, reduce state, check stop conditions\n1184: - Integration scanner discovers all surfaces an agent touches: canonical definition, runtime mirrors, command dispatch, YAML workflows, skill references\n1185: - Dynamic profiling: derives scoring rubric from any agent's own rules, no hardcoded profiles needed\n1186: - Proposal-first: candidates written to packet-local runtime areas, canonical target untouched until guarded promotion\n1187: - Guarded promotion requires passing scoring, benchmark status, repeatability evidence and operator approval. Rollback restores pre-promotion backup.\n1188: - Dimensional progress tracking detects plateau (3+ identical scores across all dimensions) and triggers stop\n1189: - All scoring is regex/string/file-existence based (no LLM-as-judge) for promotion gate reliability\n1190: - Emits `legal_stop_evaluated` and `blocked_stop` events to the JSONL ledger matching the deep-loop runtime-truth contract\n1191: - Session-boundary gate enforces fresh-session isolation before initialization\n1192: - Modes: `:auto`, `:confirm`. Supports any agent in `.opencode/agents/` as target\n1193: \n1194: **Improve Prompt**\n1195: - Refines prompts and prompt packages using 7 proven frameworks (RCAF, COSTAR, RACE, CIDI, TIDD-EC, CRISPE, CRAFT)\n1196: - Applies DEPTH thinking methodology with CLEAR quality scoring\n1197: - Used when the target already exists and needs structured improvement rather than new scaffolding\n1198: \n1199: &nbsp;\n1200: #### DOCTOR\n1201: \n1202: Three commands cover every spec-kit diagnostic surface. Run `/doctor` with no target to see the interactive menu. Upgrade users see \"Update everything to match latest release\" as option 1.\n1203: \n1204: **`/doctor <target>` (router)**\n1205: - Single entry point for 7 subsystems: `memory`, `causal-graph`, `code-graph`, `deep-loop`, `cocoindex`, `skill-advisor`, `skill-budget`\n1206: - Argv-positional dispatch via `.opencode/commands/doctor/_routes.yaml` manifest (canonical per-target metadata: setup vars, allowed flags, mutation class, MCP tools, advisor trigger phrases)\n1207: - Each target loads its own self-contained YAML workflow under `assets/doctor_<target>.yaml`\n1208: - Interactive menu when no target supplied. Tier 2 per-target prompt when a required flag is missing\n1209: - Examples: `/doctor memory --dry-run`, `/doctor causal-graph --confidence-threshold=0.8`, `/doctor code-graph --scope=stale`\n1210: - `--target=<name>` is preserved as a compatibility alias for flag-only invocation\n1211: \n1212: **`/doctor:mcp install|debug`**\n1213: - MCP infrastructure repair (replaces the standalone `/doctor:mcp_install` and `/doctor:mcp_debug` from v3.4.0.0)\n1214: - `install`. Fresh install or reinstall of the native MCP servers from their install guides. Handles old-conflicting-with-new (clean reinstall with venv/node_modules removal)\n1215: - `debug`. Diagnoses the native MCP servers (Spec Kit Memory, System Skill Advisor, System Code Graph, CocoIndex Code, Code Mode, Sequential Thinking) with PASS/WARN/FAIL per check. Supports `--fix` for guided repair\n1216: \n1217: **`/doctor:update`**\n1218: - Multi-subsystem orchestrator: dependency-safe rebuild across code-graph ŌåÆ context-index + vector-index ŌåÆ causal-edges ŌåÆ skill-graph ŌåÆ advisor ŌåÆ deep-loop ŌåÆ cocoindex ŌåÆ eval\n1219: - One lock (`mcp_server/database/.doctor-update.flock`), one pre-mutation snapshot set, one dependency DAG, one rollback policy, one state log (`.doctor-update.last-run.json`)\n1220: - Tier-aware mid-run prompts: SHORT steps auto-acknowledge. MEDIUM steps share one combined prompt (Q-MED). LONG-POLE `memory_index_scan` gets explicit ETA prompt (Q-LONG, 5-15 min)\n1221: - Additional gates: Q-PROBE (active MCP clients warning, NOT suppressed by `--force`), Q-LEGACY (per-file cleanup with `--cleanup-legacy`), Q-FAIL (step-failure recovery)\n1222: - Use after upgrading spec-kit, after large packet moves or when multiple subsystem doctors would otherwise need to run by hand. Pass `--migrate` to handle schema migration (e.g. v3.3.0.0 ŌåÆ v3.4.1.0). Wall-clock 8-25 min\n1223: \n1224: The 10 underlying YAML workflows in `.opencode/commands/doctor/assets/` are self-sufficient. Each declares its own `role/purpose/action/operating_mode/invariants/upstream_assets/user_inputs/field_handling` block plus phased execution. The `route-validate.{sh,py}` CI script enforces internal consistency on the route manifest.\n1225: \n1226: &nbsp;\n1227: #### UTILITY\n1228: \n1229: **Agent Router**\n1230: - Routes requests to external AI systems (Gemini CLI, Codex CLI, Claude Code, Copilot CLI)\n1231: - The receiving AI operates under its own system prompt - full identity adoption\n1232: - Use for cross-AI delegation where the target AI needs to behave as itself\n1233: \n1234: ---\n1235: \n1236: ### ­¤öī Code Mode MCP\n1237: \n1238: Code Mode MCP gives the AI access to external tools (Figma, GitHub, Chrome DevTools, ClickUp, Webflow) through a single TypeScript execution interface. Instead of loading large external tool definitions into context, Code Mode loads them on demand through one interface (1.6k tokens) - a 98.7% reduction.\n1239: \n1240: #### Native MCP Servers\n1241: \n1242: Canonical native server set:\n1243: \n1244: | Server                 | Tools | Purpose                                                                |\n1245: | ---------------------- | ----- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n1246: | `mk-spec-memory`      | 39    | Cognitive memory, session recovery, causal/eval tools and graph loops  |\n1247: | `mk_skill_advisor`     | 9     | Gate 2 advisor routing plus skill-graph scan/query/status/validation   |\n1248: | `mk_code_index`        | 11    | Structural code graph, `detect_changes` and CocoIndex bridge helpers   |\n1249: | `code_mode`            | 7     | External tool orchestration via TypeScript execution                   |\n1250: | `cocoindex_code`       | 2     | Semantic code search via vector embeddings                             |\n1251: | `sequential_thinking`  | 1     | Structured multi-step reasoning for complex problems                   |\n1252: | **Total**              | **69** |                                                                        |\n1253: \n1254: &nbsp;\n1255: #### Code Mode Tools (7)\n1256: \n1257: - **`search_tools`** - Discover relevant tools by task description\n1258: - **`tool_info`** - Get complete tool parameters and TypeScript interface\n1259: - **`call_tool_chain`** - Execute TypeScript code with access to all registered tools\n1260: - **`list_tools`** - List all currently registered tool names\n1261: - **`register_manual`** - Register a new tool provider\n1262: - **`deregister_manual`** - Remove a tool provider\n1263: - **`get_required_keys_for_tool`** - Check required environment variables for a tool\n1264: \n1265: &nbsp;\n1266: #### External Integrations (via `.utcp_config.json`)\n1267: \n1268: - **`chrome_devtools_1`** (MCP/stdio) - Browser automation (instance 1). No env var needed.\n1269: - **`chrome_devtools_2`** (MCP/stdio) - Browser automation (instance 2). No env var needed.\n1270: - **`clickup`** (MCP/stdio) - Task management, goals, docs. Requires `CLICKUP_API_KEY`.\n1271: - **`figma`** (MCP/stdio) - Design files, components, exports. Requires `FIGMA_API_KEY`.\n1272: - **`github`** (MCP/stdio) - Issues, pull requests, commits. Requires `GITHUB_PERSONAL_ACCESS_TOKEN`.\n1273: - **`webflow`** (MCP/remote) - Sites, CMS collections. Requires Webflow auth.\n1274: \n1275: &nbsp;\n1276: #### Performance\n1277: \n1278: | Metric            | Without Code Mode                          | With Code Mode       |\n1279: | ----------------- | ------------------------------------------ | -------------------- |\n1280: | Context tokens    | Large external tool schemas loaded upfront | 1.6k (on-demand)     |\n1281: | Round trips       | 15+ for chained operations                 | 1 (TypeScript chain) |\n1282: | Type safety       | None                                       | Full TypeScript      |\n1283: | Context reduction | -                                          | 98.7%                |\n1284: \n1285: To call a Code Mode tool: `call_tool_chain({ typescript: \"const result = await figma.figma_get_file({fileKey: 'abc123'}); return result;\" })`\n1286: \n1287: For more on the `mcp-code-mode` skill and TypeScript execution patterns, see the skill at `.opencode/skills/mcp-code-mode/SKILL.md`.\n1288: \n1289: <!-- /ANCHOR:features -->\n1290: \n1291: \n1292: <!-- ANCHOR:configuration -->\n1293: \n1294: ---\n1295: \n1296: ## 4. CONFIGURATION\n1297: \n1298: <a id=\"customizing-for-your-stack\"></a>\n1299: ### ­¤Ä» Customizing for Your Stack: Start with `sk-code`\n1300: \n1301: This repo ships as a **public template**. Of the skills it ships with, only one carries stack-specific content, start there:\n1302: \n1303: | Skill / Surface                                     | Out-of-the-box                             | Notes                                                                                                                                                                                                    |\n1304: | --------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------ | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n1305: | **`sk-code`**                                       | ­¤Ä© Stack-specific (the customization point) | Surface-aware code-quality patterns. Replace the shipped Webflow + OpenCode + Motion.dev surfaces with your own (e.g., Next.js + Tailwind + Postgres or React Native + Reanimated or Go + sqlc, etc.).   |\n1306: | `sk-doc`                                            | Ō£ģ Codebase-agnostic                        | Markdown quality + component creation. Works for any project.                                                                                                                                            |\n1307: | `sk-git`                                            | Ō£ģ Codebase-agnostic                        | Worktree + commit + PR workflow. Works for any project.                                                                                                                                                  |\n1308: | `sk-code-review`                                    | Ō£ģ Codebase-agnostic baseline               | Pulls surface evidence FROM `sk-code`. Customize `sk-code` and the review baseline auto-adapts.                                                                                                          |\n1309: | `system-spec-kit`                                   | Ō£ģ Codebase-agnostic                        | Spec folder workflow + validator + memory. Works for any project.                                                                                                                                        |\n1310: | `mcp-coco-index`                                    | Ō£ģ Codebase-agnostic                        | Semantic code search via embeddings. Works for any project.                                                                                                                                              |\n1311: | `mcp-code-mode`                                     | Ō£ģ Codebase-agnostic                        | Multi-tool MCP orchestration. Works for any project.                                                                                                                                                     |\n1312: | `deep-research` / `deep-review`                     | Ō£ģ Codebase-agnostic                        | Iterative loop protocols. Work for any topic / target.                                                                                                                                                   |\n1313: | `sk-prompt` / `deep-agent-improvement`              | Ō£ģ Codebase-agnostic                        | Prompt + agent improvement frameworks. Work for any project.                                                                                                                                             |\n1314: | `cli-*` (codex/copilot/gemini/claude-code/opencode) | Ō£ģ Codebase-agnostic                        | External CLI orchestrators. Stack-independent.                                                                                                                                                           |\n1315: | `mcp-chrome-devtools`                               | Ō£ģ Codebase-agnostic                        | Browser tooling. Stack-independent.                                                                                                                                                                      |\n1316: \n1317: **Adding your own skills:** the shipped set is intentionally minimal, most teams will add their own skills (project-specific workflows, ops runbooks, domain-specific reviewers, etc.). That's expected and supported. Just drop them into `.opencode/skills/<your-skill>/` and they'll be picked up by the advisor. The shipped skills above are kept agnostic so upstream updates apply cleanly to your fork.\n1318: \n1319: **What \"adapting `sk-code`\" looks like**:\n1320: - Replace `references/webflow/`, `references/opencode/`, `references/motion_dev/` with your stack's references (e.g., `references/nextjs/`, `references/postgres/`).\n1321: - Replace `assets/webflow/`, `assets/opencode/`, `assets/motion_dev/` with your stack's assets (checklists, recipes, snippets).\n1322: - Update `SKILL.md` ┬¦2 Smart Routing, `STACK_FOLDERS` dict + the bash detection block, to match your stack's marker files and CWD signals.\n1323: - Update the `RESOURCE_MAP` intent ŌåÆ file paths to point at your renamed references/assets.\n1324: - Bump `sk-code` version + ship a changelog. Use the `assets/opencode/checklists/skill_authoring.md` checklist as your guide.\n1325: \n1326: The other shipped skills will continue working unchanged: `sk-doc` will still validate your markdown, `sk-git` will still manage your branches, `system-spec-kit` will still spec your work and `sk-code-review` will surface YOUR `sk-code` evidence at review time.\n1327: \n1328: &nbsp;\n1329: ### Core Configuration Files\n1330: \n1331: - **`CLAUDE.md`** - Gate definitions, behavior rules, coding anti-patterns. Used by Claude Code (primary runtime).\n1332: - **`AGENTS.md`** - Agent routing, capability reference, gate documentation. Used by all runtimes.\n1333: - **`opencode.json`** - MCP server bindings, model configuration and launcher notes. Used by OpenCode platform.\n1334: - **`.utcp_config.json`** - Code Mode external tool registrations. Used by `mcp-code-mode` skill.\n1335: - **`.claude/mcp.json`** - Claude Code MCP configuration. Claude Code only.\n1336: - **`.codex/config.toml`** - Codex CLI MCP configuration and profile definitions.\n1337: - **`.gemini/settings.json`** - Gemini CLI configuration. Gemini CLI only.\n1338: - **`.vscode/mcp.json`** - VS Code / Copilot MCP configuration wrapper.\n1339: \n1340: &nbsp;\n1341: ### Memory Engine Configuration\n1342: \n1343: The memory server reads configuration from environment variables:\n1344: \n1345: - **`VOYAGE_API_KEY`** (optional) - Voyage AI cloud embeddings (opt-in only, gated by egress guard)\n1346: - **`SPECKIT_EMBEDDER`** (optional) - Override the default embedder id (default: `ollama-nomic-v1.5` since ADR-013/014 2026-05-19; was previously `ollama-jina-v3`). See [embedder-pluggability.md](.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/references/embedder-pluggability.md) for the registered list.\n1347: - **`SPECKIT_RERANK_LAYER`** (optional) - Retrieval-rescue layer toggle, default `true` per ADR-011. Set to `false` to disable.\n1348: - **`HF_EMBEDDINGS_DTYPE`** (optional) - hf-local fallback dtype (default: `q8`. Also: `fp32`, `fp16`, `q4`, `int8`, `uint8`, `bnb4`)\n1349: - **`OPENAI_API_KEY`** (optional) - OpenAI embeddings (alternative)\n1350: - **`MEMORY_DB_PATH`** (optional) - Override default database path\n1351: \n1352: Default repo-local database path: `.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/database/context-index__ollama__nomic-embed-text-v1.5__768.sqlite` (default since ADR-013/014 2026-05-19; previously `__jina-embeddings-v3__1024__q4_k_m.sqlite`). The filename encodes provider, model, dimension and dtype so multiple backends can coexist on disk without mixing vectors.\n1353: \n1354: > [!TIP]\n1355: > If no API key is set, the memory engine auto-detects the local Ollama endpoint serving **nomic-embed-text-v1.5** (current default per ADR-013/014), falls back to **jina-embeddings-v3** if nomic isn't pulled, then to **HuggingFace Local** embeddings.\n1356: \n1357: \n1358: &nbsp;\n1359: ### Memory Feature Flags\n1360: \n1361: Feature flags control search channels, scoring signals, save-time enforcement and evaluation behavior. The important retrieval/runtime flags are resolved at call time, so long-lived MCP processes do not depend on frozen import-time snapshots.\n1362: \n1363: - **Search Pipeline** - 5-channel retrieval, fallback routing, reranking, graph-walk rollout, confidence and token-budget policies.\n1364: - **Session/Cache** - Working memory, cache invalidation on DB rebind, session deduplication, recovery helpers.\n1365: - **Memory/Storage** - Save quality gate, reconsolidation, governed scopes, causal graph maintenance, projection cleanup.\n1366: - **Embedding/API** - Startup provider resolution, fail-fast dimension checks, structured fallback metadata for effective vs requested provider.\n1367: - **Evaluation/Debug** - Trace mode, eval logging, ablation/reporting guardrails, feedback evaluation and proposal diagnostics that observe candidates without reordering live results.\n1368: \n1369: For the complete flag reference with per-flag defaults, see [MCP Server README Section 5](.opencode/skills/system-spec-kit/mcp_server/README.md#5-configuration).\n1370: \n1371: &nbsp;\n1372: ### Database Schema\n1373: \n1374: The runtime centers on a SQLite `memory_index` table with 56 columns plus companion FTS5/vector, lineage, checkpoint, working-memory and eval tables.\n1375: \n\n(Output capped at 50 KB.
